is in the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222"><cite id="CITEREFMorse1863" class="citation cs2">Morse, Samuel (1863), "An Argument on the Ethical Position of Slavery in the Social System, and its Relation to the Politics of the Day", <i>New York, Papers from the Society for the Diffusion of Political Knowledge</i> (12)</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=New+York%2C+Papers+from+the+Society+for+the+Diffusion+of+Political+Knowledge&amp;rft.atitle=An+Argument+on+the+Ethical+Position+of+Slavery+in+the+Social+System%2C+and+its+Relation+to+the+Politics+of+the+Day&amp;rft.issue=12&amp;rft.date=1863&amp;rft.aulast=Morse&amp;rft.aufirst=Samuel&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASamuel+Morse" class="Z3988"></span> in <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222"><cite class="citation cs2"><i>Slavery Pamphlets # 60</i>, Beinecke Rare Book and Manuscript library, Yale University</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Slavery+Pamphlets+%23+60&amp;rft.pub=Beinecke+Rare+Book+and+Manuscript+library%2C+Yale+University&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASamuel+Morse" class="Z3988"></span> Quoted in <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222"><cite class="citation cs2"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.yaleslavery.org/WhoYaleHonors/morse.html"><i>Yale, Slavery, &amp; Abolition</i></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190921193022/http://www.yaleslavery.org/WhoYaleHonors/morse.html">archived</a> from the original on September 21, 2019<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 17,</span> 2009</span></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Yale%2C+Slavery%2C+%26+Abolition&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.yaleslavery.org%2FWhoYaleHonors%2Fmorse.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASamuel+Morse" class="Z3988"></span> \xe2\x80\x94 an online report about Yale honorees and their relation to slavery</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEStandage1998172\xe2\x80\x93173-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStandage1998172\xe2\x80\x93173_41-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFStandage1998">Standage 1998</a>, pp.&#160;172\xe2\x80\x93173.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Morse\'s actual language in his claim 8 was: "Eighth. I do not propose to limit myself to the specific machinery or parts of machinery described in the foregoing specification and claims, the essence of my invention being the use of the motive power of the electric or galvanic current, which I call electro-magnetism, however developed, for marking or printing intelligible characters, signs, or letters, at any distances, being a new application of that power of which I claim to be the first inventor or discoverer."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Supreme Court said: "Professor Morse has not discovered that the electric or galvanic current will always print at a distance, no matter what may be the form of the machinery or mechanical contrivances through which it passes. You may use electro-magnetism as a motive power, and yet not produce the described effect, that is, print at a distance intelligible marks or signs. To produce that effect, it must be combined with, and passed through, and operate upon, certain complicated and delicate machinery, adjusted and arranged upon philosophical principles, and prepared by the highest mechanical skill. And it is the high praise of Professor Morse, that he has been able, by a new combination of known powers, of which electro-magnetism is one, to discover a method by which intelligible marks or signs may be printed at a distance. And for the method or process thus discovered, he is entitled to a patent. But he has not discovered that the electro-magnetic current, used as motive power, in any other method, and with any other combination, will do as well."</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <i>O\'Reilly v. Morse</i>, 56 U.S. 62, 113, 120 (1853).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Supreme Court said, "The great difficulty in their way was the fact that the galvanic current, however strong in the beginning, became gradually weaker as it advanced on the wire; and was not strong enough to produce a mechanical effect, after a certain distance had been traversed." 56 U.S. at 107.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-46">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See, for example, <i>Alice Corporation Pty. Ltd v CLS Bank International</i>, 573 U.S. __, 134 S. Ct. 2347 (2014); <i>Mayo Collaborative Services v. Prometheus Labs., Inc.</i>, 566 U.S. __, 132 S. Ct. 1289 (2012); <i>Bilski v. Kappos</i>, 561 U.S. 593, 130 S. Ct. 3218 (2010); <i>Gottschalk v. Benson</i>, 409 U.S. 63 (1972) \xe2\x80\x93 all building on the <i>Morse</i> case as the seminal case in the field.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEStandage1998174-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStandage1998174_47-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFStandage1998">Standage 1998</a>, p.&#160;174.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1968104-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1968104_48-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFCarter1968">Carter 1968</a>, p.&#160;104.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1968123-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1968123_49-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFCarter1968">Carter 1968</a>, p.&#160;123.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1968149-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1968149_50-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFCarter1968">Carter 1968</a>, p.&#160;149.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEStandage1998189-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStandage1998189_51-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFStandage1998">Standage 1998</a>, p.&#160;189.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-52">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ridgefieldnj.gov/?SEC=9842071E-0EBB-4CC1-A535-56CF6832C4A8">"History of Ridgefield \xe2\x80\x93 Ridgefield, New Jersey"</a>. <i>www.ridgefieldnj.gov</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">November 29,</span> 2019</span>. <q>Among the noted people who owned property in the new borough was Samuel F. B. Morse. He owned property running from Morse Avenue east to Dallytown Road (Bergen Boulevard). Morse bought the property with the intention of building a home here.
